              Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is
              the summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
              models the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on
              a single tissue using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan needs individual-level data to
              fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

            $$

            \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

            $$ {#eq:predixcan}


            where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
            coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
            $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
            assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
            \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$.

            summary statistics with the expression


            $$

            \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l

            $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


            where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$
            is the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$,
            and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the
            GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances
            are always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project
            (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel.

            confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
            drug repurposing approach (described below).

              statistics with the expression:

              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for
              each gene's tissue model $l$. S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics with the expression:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ signifies the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ denotes the variance of the predicted expression
              of a gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ represents the
              estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS
              methods, genotype variances and covariances are consistently
              estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel.
              S-PrediXcan's tissue-specific direction of effects, such as
              whether higher or lower predicted gene expression confers greater
              or lesser disease risk, enabled us to incorporate the $z$-scores
              into our drug repurposing approach (detailed below).

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
              regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of this
              association is determined by computing the $z$-score (Equation 2):


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l),

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              for each gene's tissue-specific model $l$.


              3. **Data Requirements and Approximations**: PrediXcan requires
              individual-level data for fitting this model, while S-PrediXcan
              approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary
              statistics with the expression:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ denotes the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted gene expression
              in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ represents the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.

              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.


              In these TWAS methods, genotype variances and covariances are
              consistently estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression
              project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference
              panel. S-PrediXcan's advantage lies in its ability to provide
              tissue-specific direction of effects, such as whether a higher or
              lower predicted gene expression confers more or less disease risk.
              As a result, we employed the $z$-scores in our drug repurposing
              approach (detailed below).

              Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is
              the summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
              models the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on
              a single tissue using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan needs individual-level data to
              fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our

              1. S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a simplified
              version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models a trait
              as a linear function based on a single tissue's gene expression
              using the univariate model:


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
              tissue $l$, $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The association's significance
              is determined by calculating the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for
              each gene's tissue model $l$.


              S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS
              summary statistics and the expression:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted gene expression
              in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of
              SNP $a$ from the GWAS.


              In these TWAS methods, genotype variances and covariances are
              consistently estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression
              project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference
              panel. Since S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific directions of
              effects (e.g., whether higher or lower predicted gene expression
              confers more or less disease risk), we utilized the $z$-scores in
              our drug repurposing approach (detailed below).

              S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS

              where $\mathbf{t}_l$ is the predicted gene expression in tissue

              $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The association's significance is

              $$ {#eq:z_score}

              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted gene expression

              Expression project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the

              in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of

              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel for estimating
              genotype variances and covariances. S-PrediXcan provides
              tissue-specific direction of effects, which is useful in our drug
              repurposing approach (described below).

              Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is
              the summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
              models the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on
              a single tissue using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where \mathbf{t}_l is the gene predicted expression in tissue $l$,
              $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient,
              and $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
              $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
              assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
              \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$.
              PrediXcan needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas
              S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS
              summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a condensed
              version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models a trait
              as a linear function of gene expression in a single tissue using
              the univariate model:


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
              tissue $l$, $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The association's significance
              is evaluated by calculating the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. S-PrediXcan, in contrast to PrediXcan,
              approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary
              statistics:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}

              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a

              variances and covariances are consistently estimated using the

              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. As

              S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS
              summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              Failed to fix the following expressions:
               - $\hat{\beta}_l$ -> $\hat{\beta}_a$

              1. **S-PrediXcan** [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a
              simplified version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. In
              S-PrediXcan, the trait is modeled as a linear function of gene
              expression in a single tissue using the univariate model:


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\mathbf{t}_l$ represents the predicted gene expression in
              tissue $l$, $\gamma_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The association's significance
              is evaluated by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\frac{\hat{\gamma}_l}{\text{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)}$ for
              a gene's tissue model $l$.


              Unlike PrediXcan, S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores
              using only GWAS summary statistics with the expression:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\text{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted gene expression
              in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of
              SNP $a$ from the GWAS. 


              In these TWAS methods, genotype variances and covariances are
              consistently estimated using GTEx v8
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel. S-PrediXcan's
              advantage is that it provides tissue-specific directions of
              effects (e.g., whether higher or lower predicted gene expression
              confers more or less disease risk), which we utilized in our drug
              repurposing approach (described below).

              Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is
              the summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
              models the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on
              a single tissue using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where \mathbf{t}_l is the gene predicted expression in tissue $l$,
              $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient,
              and $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
              $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
              assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
              \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$.
              PrediXcan needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas
              S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS
              summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

            text: >-
              Failed to fix the following expressions:
               - \appro  -> \approx 
               - \mathbf{t_l  -> \mathbf{t}_l 
              ---

              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a streamlined
              version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models a trait
              as a linear function of gene expression in a single tissue using
              the univariate model:


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The association's significance
              is evaluated by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$.


              S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS
              summary statistics and the expression:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.


              In these TWAS methods, genotype variances and covariances are
              consistently estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression
              project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference
              panel. S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects,
              such as whether a higher or lower predicted gene expression
              confers more or less disease risk, which is crucial for our drug
              repurposing approach (described in detail below).

              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype

              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)

              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for

              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is
              the summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
              models the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on
              a single tissue using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan needs individual-level data to
              fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              1. S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is a simplified
              version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models a trait
              as a linear function of a gene's expression in a single tissue
              using the univariate model:


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The association's significance
              is assessed by calculating the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. Unlike PrediXcan, S-PrediXcan
              approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary
              statistics with the expression:


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. 


              In these TWAS methods, genotype variances and covariances are
              consistently estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression
              project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference
              panel. S-PrediXcan's advantage is its ability to provide
              tissue-specific direction of effects, indicating whether higher or
              lower predicted gene expression confers more or less disease risk.
              As a result, we employed the $z$-scores in our drug repurposing
              approach (detailed below).
